Dear Mr. Atta: 
In accordance with the Agreement for Consulting Services entered into on 
August 14, 2014 with AMX Partners LLC, Geolabs observed the foundation installation 
operations for the Park Lane Ala Moana (Commercial Parking) project at the Ala Moana 
Center in Honolulu on the Island of Oahu, Hawaii. The foundation for the new parking 
structure project consists of 1,441 augered cast-in-place (ACIP) piles supporting the 
new development. 
The ACIP pile foundation installation work spanned from September 6, 2014 
through February 6, 2015. Geolabs also observed the performance of static 
compressive load tests on two sacrificial 18-inch diameter ACIP piles.  
To the best of our knowledge, it is our professional opinion that the foundation 
installation work for the Park Lane Ala Moana (Commercial Parking) project observed by 
Geolabs has been constructed in general conformance with the approved plans and 
specifications, our geotechnical engineering report prepared for the project, and 
subsequent recommendations to accommodate the encountered field conditions. The 
constructed ACIP pile foundations observed by Geolabs should be capable of providing 
the design load capacities.

ACIP Pile Foundation Installation Observation Report

Reference: Report by Geolabs, Inc. dated June 25, 2014 
entitled "Geotechnical Engineering Exploration 
Park Lane Ala Moana

Building Permit No.: 751924 
Dear Mr. Pollock: 
In accordance with the Agreement for Consulting Services entered into on 
August 14, 2014 with AMX Partners LLC, Geolabs observed the performance of two static 
load tests, load test pile installation, and production pile operations for the augered 
cast-in-place (ACIP) pile foundations for the Park Lane Ala Moana (Commercial Parking) 
project in Honolulu on the Island of Oahu, Hawaii. This letter report summarizes our 
geotechnical observations during the ACIP pile foundation installation for the project.  
Geolabs provided geotechnical engineering consultation for the Park Lane 
Ala Moana project, and the findings and recommendations are presented in the referenced 
report. The purpose of our geotechnical observations was to monitor the geotechnical 
engineering aspects of the ACIP pile foundation installation for conformance with the intent 
of the recommendations presented in our report. In addition, we provided “Special 
Inspection” services (as required by the City and Country of Honolulu) by observing the 
ACIP pile foundation installation for general conformance with the project plans and 
specifications. 
Page 2 
Rider Levett Bucknall 
W.O. 6945-10 (ACIP Pile Foundation Installation Observation Report) 
January 22, 2016 
GEOLABS, INC. 
Hawaii • California 
PROJECT DESCRIPTION 
In general, the Park Lane Ala Moana project involves expansion of the makai 
(southern) portion of the shopping center by demolishing the existing parking deck in this 
area and constructing a three-level parking structure below multi-level residential 
condominium structures. The site is generally bounded by Neiman Marcus to the east, 
Ala Moana Boulevard to the south, Piikoi Street to the west, and the existing mall and mall 
expansion to the north. The general project vicinity is shown on the Project Location Map, 
Plate 1. 
Based on the geotechnical engineering report referenced above for the project, we 
recommended supporting the new condominium and parking structures on a deep 
foundation system consisting of 18-inch diameter augered cast-in-place piles with 
allowable compressive load capacities of 300, 400, and 500 kips per pile. Most of the 
ACIP piles would extend through the soft and/or loose lagoonal deposits (near the surface) 
and derive support primarily from skin friction and end-bearing within coral ledges and/or 
coralline detritus materials encountered below the lagoonal deposit. The typical ACIP pile 
lengths would be about 60, 70, and 78 feet for the 300, 400, and 500-kip capacity piles, 
respectively. The general contractor for the project was Albert C. Kobayashi, Inc. (ACK), 
and the ACIP pile installation subcontractor was Hawaiian Dredging Construction 
Company, Inc. (HDCC). 
STATIC PILE LOAD TEST 
In order to evaluate the adequacy of the recommended design lengths of the 
ACIP pile foundation, static pile load tests were conducted on two dedicated ACIP piles on 
November 25 and 26, 2014 and December 19, 2014. The pile load tests were conducted 
on two 18-inch diameter ACIP piles with lengths of approximately 75 feet relative to the 
existing ground surface. To better understand the load transfer mechanism at the pile-soil 
interface, the load test piles were instrumented with seven vibrating wire embedment strain 
gages installed at various depths along the length of each load test pile. 
A Bauer BG-28 drill rig equipped with automatic monitoring equipment and a 
continuous flight hollow-stem auger was used to install the test piles. A hydraulic concrete 
pump with an average stroke volume of about 0.067 cubic yard per stroke was used to 
pump the grout into the pile system. The test pile was loaded in general accordance with 
ASTM D1143, Quick Load Test Method. The maximum test load on the piles were 
1,036 kips. The static pile load test results are summarized in the report entitled “ACIP Pile 
Load Test Report, Park Lane Ala Moana, Honolulu, Oahu, Hawaii” dated January 23, 2015. 
Based on the static pile load test results, it appeared the load test piles generally 
behaved like friction piles with nearly 100 percent of the maximum test loads being 
resisted by adhesion between the ACIP pile and the surrounding soils. Based on our field 
observations and the results of the static pile load tests, we confirmed the design 
embedment lengths would be sufficient to achieve the design compressive load capacities 
Rider Levett Bucknall 
Page 3 
W.O. 6945-10 (ACIP Pile Foundation Installation Observation Report) 
January 22, 2016 
GEOLABS, INC. 
Hawaii • California 
of 300, 400, and 500 kips per pile for the 60, 70, and 78-foot deep piles, respectively, with 
a factor of safety of at least 2.0.  
PRODUCTION PILE INSTALLATION 
The production ACIP pile installation program, consisting of installing 1,441 ACIP 
piles, was conducted from September 6, 2014 through February 6, 2015 under the 
near-continuous (full-time) observations by a field engineer from our office. In addition to 
the Bauer BG-28 drill rig utilized for the test pile program, HDCC used a Manitowoc 12000 
series crane with a crane-mounted hollow-stem auger powered by an APE 75C Hydraulic 
pump to install the production piles. Automatic monitoring equipment was mounted on the 
drilling/pumping equipment with the intent of providing auger depth, grout flow rate, grout 
pressure, etc., on a near-continuous basis.  
During the pile installation operation, logs were maintained for each ACIP pile, 
which included information pertaining to pile number, date installed, depth of pile, grout 
volume used, grout return depth, etc. The locations of the production ACIP piles installed 
are shown on the ACIP Pile Identification Plans, Plates 2.1 through 2.8. The production 
ACIP pile installation summary is presented by pile number on Plates 3.1 through 3.57 of 
this letter report. 
Based on our observation of the equipment performance and subsurface conditions 
encountered, it is our professional opinion that the production ACIP piles have been 
installed to sufficient depths and/or resistance to provide the design load capacities of 300, 
400, and 500 kips per pile with a safety factor of 2.0. 
LIMITATIONS 
It should be noted that it is not possible to continuously observe all activities 
occurring simultaneously on a construction site even when our representatives are on the 
project site on a full-time basis. Our observation and consultation services were performed 
in accordance with generally accepted standards of geotechnical engineering practice; no 
warranty is expressed or implied. Provision of construction monitoring by an engineer is 
not insurance, nor does it guarantee construction of any type. The contractor shall retain 
primary responsibility for the quality of the work, for adhering to plans and specifications, 
and for repairing defects regardless of when they are found.
